<td class="noprint" colspan="2" style="text-align:center"><img alt="" data-file-height="60" data-file-width="60" height="33" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/ce/Soccerball_current_event.svg/33px-Soccerball_current_event.svg.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/ce/Soccerball_current_event.svg/50px-Soccerball_current_event.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/ce/Soccerball_current_event.svg/66px-Soccerball_current_event.svg.png 2x" width="33"/> <i><a href="/wiki/2016%E2%80%9317_Real_Oviedo_season" title="2016–17 Real Oviedo season">Current season</a></i></td>

<p><b>Real Oviedo</b> (<a href="/wiki/Asturian_language" title="Asturian language">Asturian</a>: <span lang="ast" xml:lang="ast"><i>Real Uviéu</i></span>) is a <a href="/wiki/List_of_football_clubs_in_Spain" title="List of football clubs in Spain">Spanish football club</a> based in <a href="/wiki/Oviedo" title="Oviedo">Oviedo</a>, in the autonomous community of <a href="/wiki/Asturias" title="Asturias">Asturias</a>. Founded on 26 March 1926 as a result of the merger of two clubs who had maintained a large sporting rivalry for years in the city: <i>Real Stadium Club Ovetense</i> and <i>Real Club Deportivo Oviedo</i>. The club plays in the <a href="/wiki/Segunda_Divisi%C3%B3n" title="Segunda División">Segunda División</a>, the second tier of the <a href="/wiki/Spanish_football_league_system" title="Spanish football league system">Spanish football league system</a>.</p>
<p>The club plays in blue shirts and white shorts in the <a href="/wiki/Estadio_Carlos_Tartiere" title="Estadio Carlos Tartiere">Estadio Carlos Tartiere</a>, which seats 30,500 spectators, opened on 30 September 2000, is the largest sports stadium in Asturias. In the <a href="/wiki/La_Liga#All-time_La_Liga_table" title="La Liga">all-time league table</a> for the Spanish top division, Oviedo rank in 17th place.</p>
<p></p>

<p></p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="History">History</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Real_Oviedo&amp;action=edit&amp;section=1" title="Edit section: History">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<p>Founded in 1926 after a <a href="/wiki/Mergers_and_acquisitions" title="Mergers and acquisitions">merger</a> with <i>Stadium Ovetense</i> and <i>Real Club Deportivo Oviedo</i>, Oviedo first reached <a href="/wiki/La_Liga" title="La Liga">La Liga</a> seven years later.</p>
<div class="thumb tleft">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:122px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Langara.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="800" data-file-width="581" height="165" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/ca/Langara.jpg/120px-Langara.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/ca/Langara.jpg/180px-Langara.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/ca/Langara.jpg/240px-Langara.jpg 2x" width="120"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Langara.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Lángara won three consecutive Pichichi trophies from 1933-34 to 1935-36.</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>Their attacking quartet of <a href="/wiki/Emil%C3%ADn" title="Emilín">Emilín</a>, Galé, <a href="/wiki/Eduardo_Herrera_Bueno" title="Eduardo Herrera Bueno">Herrerita</a> and <a href="/wiki/Isidro_L%C3%A1ngara" title="Isidro Lángara">Isidro Lángara</a> (all represented <a href="/wiki/Spain_national_football_team" title="Spain national football team">Spain</a> in this period), as well as Casuco and Ricardo Gallart modernised the game with their pace and running off the ball tied with sharp passing and one-touch football, played in a style 30/40 years before its time, being dubbed <i>Delanteras Eléctricas</i> ("The electric forwards"); all this was connected with a rigid training and fitness regime started by a former manager of the club, Englishman <a href="/wiki/Fred_Pentland" title="Fred Pentland">Fred Pentland</a>.</p>
<p>Lángara won the <a href="/wiki/Pichichi_Trophy" title="Pichichi Trophy">Pichichi Trophy</a> three years in a row prior to the <a href="/wiki/Spanish_Civil_War" title="Spanish Civil War">Spanish Civil War</a>, as Oviedo broke all scoring records (174 goals in 62 league games). With the outbreak of the conflict, however, the team broke up: Lángara emigrated to <a href="/wiki/South_America" title="South America">South America</a>, Herrerita and Emilín signed with <a href="/wiki/FC_Barcelona" title="FC Barcelona">FC Barcelona</a>, Galé with <a href="/wiki/Racing_de_Santander" title="Racing de Santander">Racing de Santander</a> and Gallart with <a href="/wiki/Racing_de_Ferrol" title="Racing de Ferrol">Racing de Ferrol</a>.</p>
<p>When football in the country resumed in 1939, Oviedo were relegated to the <a href="/wiki/Segunda_Divisi%C3%B3n" title="Segunda División">second division</a>, as their pitch was deemed unplayable – <a href="/wiki/Francisco_Franco" title="Francisco Franco">Francisco Franco</a>'s troops had used the stadium as an ammunition dump. During the following decades, the club bounced back between the first (38 seasons) and second levels (32), the high point being qualifying for the <a href="/wiki/UEFA_Europa_League" title="UEFA Europa League">UEFA Cup</a> after finishing a best-ever third in <a href="/wiki/1962%E2%80%9363_La_Liga" title="1962–63 La Liga">1962–63</a> (ranking joint-first with <a href="/wiki/Real_Madrid_C.F." title="Real Madrid C.F.">Real Madrid</a> after the first 15 rounds), while the lowest was the side's first relegation to <i><a href="/wiki/Segunda_Divisi%C3%B3n_B" title="Segunda División B">Segunda División B</a></i>, in 1978 (for a single season).</p>
<p>With the <a href="/wiki/FIFA_World_Cup" title="FIFA World Cup">FIFA World Cup</a> to be held <a href="/wiki/1982_FIFA_World_Cup" title="1982 FIFA World Cup">on home soil in 1982</a>, the <i><a href="/wiki/Estadio_Carlos_Tartiere_(1932)" title="Estadio Carlos Tartiere (1932)">Carlos Tartiere Stadium</a></i> was completely renewed, the first match being held with the <a href="/wiki/Chile_national_football_team" title="Chile national football team">Chilean national team</a> (0–0). In 1984–85 Oviedo won the soon-to-be-defunct <a href="/wiki/Copa_de_la_Liga" title="Copa de la Liga">Spanish League Cup</a> (second division), after successively defeating <a href="/wiki/UD_Salamanca" title="UD Salamanca">UD Salamanca</a>, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Bilbao_Athletic" title="Bilbao Athletic">Bilbao Athletic</a>, <a href="/wiki/C.F._Lorca_Deportiva_(1969)" title="C.F. Lorca Deportiva (1969)">CF Lorca Deportiva</a>, <a href="/wiki/CE_Sabadell_FC" title="CE Sabadell FC">CE Sabadell FC</a> and <a href="/wiki/Atl%C3%A9tico_Madrid_B" title="Atlético Madrid B">Atlético Madrileño</a> (the latter with a 2–1 aggregate in the final).</p>
<p>In 1988 Oviedo returned to the top division, after ousting <a href="/wiki/RCD_Mallorca" title="RCD Mallorca">RCD Mallorca</a> in the promotion playoffs (2–1 on aggregate, with <a href="/wiki/Forward_(association_football)" title="Forward (association football)">striker</a> <a href="/wiki/Carlos_Mu%C3%B1oz_Cobo" title="Carlos Muñoz Cobo">Carlos</a>, who would feature prominently for the club in the following years, scoring one of the goals), and remained in that level for 13 consecutive seasons – in <a href="/wiki/1990%E2%80%9391_La_Liga" title="1990–91 La Liga">1990–91</a> it finished sixth, <a href="/wiki/1991%E2%80%9392_UEFA_Cup" title="1991–92 UEFA Cup">qualifying</a> once again for Europe, and being knocked out in the first round by <a href="/wiki/Genoa_C.F.C." title="Genoa C.F.C.">Genoa C.F.C.</a> of <a href="/wiki/Italy" title="Italy">Italy</a> (2–3, although Oviedo bounced back from that defeat immediately, with a 2–1 win at the <a href="/wiki/Camp_Nou" title="Camp Nou">Camp Nou</a> over Barcelona).<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-1"><a href="#cite_note-1">[1]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-2"><a href="#cite_note-2">[2]</a></sup></p>
<p>After that successful year, there were more brilliant seasons and others where relegation was narrowly dodged (in 1998 Real Oviedo succeeded in a <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/1997-98_La_Liga#Relegation_playoff" title="1997-98 La Liga">relegation playoff</a> to stay up after beating <a href="/wiki/UD_Las_Palmas" title="UD Las Palmas">UD Las Palmas</a>). In a nutshell, the <i>Carbayones</i> had an outstanding run in La Liga during the 1990s with a team which lined up top international players. In 1992 Real Oviedo as well as most Spanish football clubs were forced to become <a href="/wiki/Sociedad_An%C3%B3nima_Deportiva" title="Sociedad Anónima Deportiva">public limited sports companies</a>. The initial capital stock for Real Oviedo amounted to €3.6 million.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-3"><a href="#cite_note-3">[3]</a></sup></p>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:232px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Estadio_Carlos_Tartiere_2008.JPG"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1920" data-file-width="2560" height="173" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/17/Estadio_Carlos_Tartiere_2008.JPG/230px-Estadio_Carlos_Tartiere_2008.JPG" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/17/Estadio_Carlos_Tartiere_2008.JPG/345px-Estadio_Carlos_Tartiere_2008.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/17/Estadio_Carlos_Tartiere_2008.JPG/460px-Estadio_Carlos_Tartiere_2008.JPG 2x" width="230"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Estadio_Carlos_Tartiere_2008.JPG" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
<a href="/wiki/Estadio_Carlos_Tartiere" title="Estadio Carlos Tartiere">Carlos Tartiere Stadium</a></div>
</div>
</div>
<p>In 2000, the new <i><a href="/wiki/Estadio_Carlos_Tartiere" title="Estadio Carlos Tartiere">Carlos Tartiere Stadium</a></i> with 30,500 seats became Real Oviedo’s new ground. It was officially opened on 20 September 2000 with a match between Real Oviedo and <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Partizan_Belgrade" title="Partizan Belgrade">Partizan Belgrade</a>, where Real Oviedo lost 0-2 to the Serbian side. Three days before, Real Oviedo and UD Las Palmas had got a 2-2 draw on the first fixture in the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/2000-01_La_Liga" title="2000-01 La Liga">2000–01 season</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-4"><a href="#cite_note-4">[4]</a></sup></p>
<p>After being relegated two consecutive times, Real Oviedo suffered severe economic troubles, which, when coupled with a profound lack of institutional support from the city's government, resulted in the team's inability to pay its players. The club was then forced to drop all the way to the <a href="/wiki/Tercera_Divisi%C3%B3n" title="Tercera División">fourth division</a> of <a href="/wiki/Spanish_football_league_system" title="Spanish football league system">Spanish football</a>, for the <a href="/wiki/2003%E2%80%9304_Tercera_Divisi%C3%B3n" title="2003–04 Tercera División">2003–04 season</a>; at this point the team nearly folded but eventually recovered and regrouped, returning to level three in the following campaign.</p>
<p>Oviedo lasted two further campaigns before dropping down a level again. In another playoff against a Mallorca team – this time <a href="/wiki/RCD_Mallorca_B" title="RCD Mallorca B">the reserves</a>, the club returned again to the third division, after a <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Penalty_shootout_(association_football)" title="Penalty shootout (association football)">penalty shootout</a>; however, its survival remained at risk in the following years, due to continuing financial difficulties.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-5"><a href="#cite_note-5">[5]</a></sup></p>
<p>The financial dire straits continued into the <a href="/wiki/2012%E2%80%9313_Segunda_Divisi%C3%B3n_B" title="2012–13 Segunda División B">2012–13 season</a>, when Oviedo called on supporters to buy shares in the club. A few footballers, notably <a href="/wiki/Santi_Cazorla" title="Santi Cazorla">Santi Cazorla</a>, <a href="/wiki/Juan_Mata" title="Juan Mata">Juan Mata</a>, <a href="/wiki/Michu" title="Michu">Michu</a> and <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Adri%C3%A1n_L%C3%B3pez_%C3%81lvarez" title="Adrián López Álvarez">Adrián</a> who all started their careers there, offered their financial support in an attempt to save the club from bankruptcy – the club had until 17 November to raise <a href="/wiki/Euro" title="Euro">€</a>2 million in order to prevent closure.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-6"><a href="#cite_note-6">[6]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-7"><a href="#cite_note-7">[7]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-8"><a href="#cite_note-8">[8]</a></sup></p>
<p>On 17 November 2012 <a href="/wiki/Carlos_Slim" title="Carlos Slim">Carlos Slim</a>, the second richest man in the world, invested <a href="/wiki/United_States_dollar" title="United States dollar">$</a>2.5 million in the club, therefore gaining a controlling stake.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-9"><a href="#cite_note-9">[9]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-10"><a href="#cite_note-10">[10]</a></sup></p>
<p>On 31 May 2015, Oviedo confirmed their return to the Spanish <a href="/wiki/Segunda_Divisi%C3%B3n" title="Segunda División">Segunda División</a> after a thirteen-year absence with a 2–1 aggregate victory over <a href="/wiki/C%C3%A1diz_CF" title="Cádiz CF">Cádiz</a> in the <a href="/wiki/2015_Segunda_Divisi%C3%B3n_B_play-offs" title="2015 Segunda División B play-offs">2015 Segunda División B play-offs</a>.</p>

<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Individual">Individual</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Real_Oviedo&amp;action=edit&amp;section=7" title="Edit section: Individual">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Pichichi_Trophy">Pichichi Trophy</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Real_Oviedo&amp;action=edit&amp;section=8" title="Edit section: Pichichi Trophy">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<ul>
<li><b><a href="/wiki/La_Liga" title="La Liga">La Liga</a>:</b> <a href="/wiki/Isidro_L%C3%A1ngara" title="Isidro Lángara">Isidro Lángara</a> <b>(3)</b> (1933–34, 1934–35, 1935–36), <a href="/wiki/Marian%C3%ADn" title="Marianín">Marianín</a> (1972–73)</li>
<li><b><a href="/wiki/Segunda_Divisi%C3%B3n" title="Segunda División">Segunda División</a>:</b> Isidro Lángara (1932–33), Eduardo Gómez "Lalo" (1957–58), <a href="/wiki/Enrique_Gal%C3%A1n" title="Enrique Galán">Galán</a> (1971–72), <a href="/wiki/Carlos_Mu%C3%B1oz_Cobo" title="Carlos Muñoz Cobo">Carlos</a> (1987–88)</li>
<li><b><a href="/wiki/Segunda_Divisi%C3%B3n_B" title="Segunda División B">Segunda División B</a>:</b> <a href="/wiki/Miguel_Linares" title="Miguel Linares">Miguel Linares</a> (2014-15)</li>
<li><b><a href="/wiki/Tercera_Divisi%C3%B3n" title="Tercera División">Tercera División</a>:</b> <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Diego_Cervero_Otero" title="Diego Cervero Otero">Diego Cervero</a> <b>(3)</b> (2004–05, 2007–08, 2008–09)</li>
</ul>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Zamora_Trophy">Zamora Trophy</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Real_Oviedo&amp;action=edit&amp;section=9" title="Edit section: Zamora Trophy">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<ul>
<li><b><a href="/wiki/Segunda_Divisi%C3%B3n" title="Segunda División">Segunda División</a>:</b> Óscar Álvarez <b>(2)</b> (1931–32, 1932–33), Lombardía (1971–72)</li>
<li><b><a href="/wiki/Tercera_Divisi%C3%B3n" title="Tercera División">Tercera División</a>:</b> <a href="/wiki/Rafael_Ponzo" title="Rafael Ponzo">Rafael Ponzo</a> (2003–04), <a href="/wiki/Oinatz_Aulestia" title="Oinatz Aulestia">Oinatz Aulestia</a> (2008–09)</li>
</ul>

<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Rivalries">Rivalries</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Real_Oviedo&amp;action=edit&amp;section=15" title="Edit section: Rivalries">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<p>The <a href="/wiki/Asturian_derby" title="Asturian derby">Asturian derby</a> has been closely contested throughout its history and the two teams have met 117 times in all competitions. Real Oviedo have won 49 times, while <a href="/wiki/Sporting_de_Gij%C3%B3n" title="Sporting de Gijón">Sporting de Gijón</a> have done so in 38 games; 30 draws have been produced.</p>
<p>Sporting won the first match ever played, a 2–1 win for the Regional Championships on 6 December 1926. The first top flight derby took place during the <a href="/wiki/1944%E2%80%9345_La_Liga" title="1944–45 La Liga">1944–45 season</a>, and honours were split over the two games: Oviedo won its home fixture 2–1, but lost by a record 0–6 at <a href="/wiki/El_Molin%C3%B3n" title="El Molinón">El Molinón</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-12"><a href="#cite_note-12">[12]</a></sup></p>
<p>The inaugural second level season, <a href="/wiki/1929_Segunda_Divisi%C3%B3n" title="1929 Segunda División">1929</a>, also brought two local derbies – Oviedo thrashed Sporting 6–2 at home, while Sporting won 3–2 in the return fixture. On 15 March 1998, in the top level, the last contest took place, and Oviedo emerged victorious 2–1 at the Tartiere, eventually managing to stay afloat (only through the play-offs though) whilst the <i>Rojiblancos</i> <a href="/wiki/1997%E2%80%9398_La_Liga" title="1997–98 La Liga">suffered direct relegation</a> as 20th and last.</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Supporters">Supporters</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Real_Oviedo&amp;action=edit&amp;section=16" title="Edit section: Supporters">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<p>After the first relegation in its history to <a href="/wiki/Tercera_Divisi%C3%B3n" title="Tercera División">Tercera División</a>, <a href="/wiki/2003%E2%80%9304_Tercera_Divisi%C3%B3n" title="2003–04 Tercera División">2003–04 season</a>, the historical record of the category was established with 10,759 season ticket holders, up to that time, the record was for <a href="/wiki/M%C3%A1laga_CF" title="Málaga CF">Málaga CF</a> in 1995 with 4,200.</p>
<p>5,200 members are kept since 2001, when Real Oviedo was relegated from <a href="/wiki/La_Liga" title="La Liga">La Liga</a> and achieved its particular record of 19,132 season ticket holders.</p>

<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Real_Oviedo_B">Real Oviedo B</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Real_Oviedo&amp;action=edit&amp;section=18" title="Edit section: Real Oviedo B">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<p>The <a href="/wiki/Reserve_team" title="Reserve team">reserve team</a>, which played since 2010 in the fourth level, was renamed <i><a href="/wiki/Real_Oviedo_Vetusta" title="Real Oviedo Vetusta">Real Oviedo Vetusta</a></i> in 2008. Vetusta was also the original name of the team, before the <a href="/wiki/Royal_Spanish_Football_Federation" title="Royal Spanish Football Federation">Royal Spanish Football Federation</a> decree which banned unique reserve club names in the early 1990s.</p>
